рд╡рд╛рдорджреЗрд╡реНрдпреЗ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереЗ рдордгреНрдбрд▓реЗ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрд╛рдГ ред рддрддреНрд░ рдкреНрд░рдердореЗрд╜рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХреЗ рджрд╢ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рдирд┐ ред рддреЗрд╖реБ ’ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рд╣реНрдпрдЧреНрдиреЗ рд╕рджрдорд┐рддреН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрдпреГрдЪрдВ рдкреНрд░рдердордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдореН ред рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдпрдордиреБрдХреНрд░рдордгрд┐рдХрд╛- рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рд╣реНрдпрдЧреНрдиреЗ рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддрд┐рд░рд╖реНрдЯреНрдпрддрд┐рдЬрдЧрддреАрдзреГрддрдп рдЖрджреНрдпрд╛ рдЙрдкрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рд╢реНрдЪрддрд╕реНрд░реЛ рд╡рд╛рд░реБрдгреНрдпрд╢реНрдЪ рд╡рд╛ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдордиреНрддреНрд░рджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рд╡рд╛рдорджреЗрд╡ рдЛрд╖рд┐рдГ ред рдкреНрд░рдердорд╛ рдЪрддреБрдГрд╖рд╖реНрдЯреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд░рд╛рд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдГ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрд╛ рджреНрд╡рд┐рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд╢рджрдХреНрд╖рд░рд╛рддрд┐рдЬрдЧрддреА рддреГрддреАрдпрд╛ рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╕рдкреНрддрддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд░рд╛ рдзреГрддрд┐рд╢реНрдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереНрдпрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛ рдЕрдирд╛рджреЗрд╢рдкрд░рд┐рднрд╛рд╖рдпрд╛ рд╕рдкреНрддрджрд╢ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГред рдХреГрддреНрд╕реНрдирд╕реНрдп рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╕реНрдп тАЬ рдордгреНрдбрд▓рд╛рджрд┐рд╖реНрд╡рд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрдпрдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрд░рд┐рднрд╛рд╖рдпрд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ рджреНрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рд╢реНрдЪрддрд╕реНрд░реЛ рд╡рд░реБрдгрджреЗрд╡рддреНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд╛ ред рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рд▓реИрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдХрдГ ред рдЖрджреНрдпрд╛ рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЛрдкрд╛рдХрд░рдгреЗ рдордгреНрдбрд▓рд╛рджрд┐рд╣реЛрдореЗ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛ рее

+Jamison Brereton

1 (297)
Agni
V─Бmadeva Gautama
20 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except aс╣гс╣нi 1, atijagat─л 2, dhrti 3 ╠е
This long and complex hymn contains an important account of the Vala myth: the opening of the cave containing the imprisoned cows and their release. Although the

hero of this myth is, of course, ordinarily Indra, he does not appear in the hymn, even in disguised fashion. Instead, the troop that usually aids him in this exploit, the Aс╣Еgirases, receive all the credit, though they are not mentioned by name. The absence of Indra can presumably be ascribed to the fact that this is a hymn to Agni; the larger question is why the Vala myth is appropriate to an Agni hymn. Here the answer must be the connection of both gods with the dawn: the ruddy Vala cows are regularly identified as the dawns, and the ritual fire is kindled at dawn. Indeed the Vala myth in this hymn is introduced by a reference to AgniтАЩs primordial birth (vs. 11), and the (unnamed) Aс╣Еgirases are identified as his begetters (vs. 12): perhaps they free the embryonic Agni enclosed тАЬin the nest of the bullтАЭ (vss. 11тАУ12) as they do the Vala cows. We have seen the connection between the birth of the ritual fire and the Vala myth elsewhere, for example, in III.31, an Indra hymn, where it was also mediated by dawn.
The Vala myth is embedded within verses more conventionally devoted to Agni. The first five verses address Agni directly. He is first reminded of his original instal lation by the gods and their purpose in so doing (vs. 1), and in the next four verses Agni is urged to use his closeness to Varuс╣Зa in order to intercede for us mortals with that god. The next four verses praise Agni in the 3rd person, concentrating on his present state. Verses 10тАУ12 form the transition to the Vala myth; in fact verse 10 might seem to go naturally with 6тАУ9, but, with its reference to the treasure of the gods, it forms a ring with verse 18, which closes the Vala section. The heart of the Vala narrative consists of verses 13тАУ17. The final two verses (19тАУ20) provide a summarizing praise of Agni.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Agni I do not understand the emphasis on Varuс╣Зa in the early parts of the hymn (vss. 2-5; see also 18d), since the Vala myth and the unnamed Aс╣Еgirases in the later parts of the hymn have no obvious conceptual connection with Varuс╣Зa and the ─Аdityas (see also Aditi in 20a).

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬSince the emulous gods ever excite you, Agni, who are a deity swift of motion, (to contest), therefore do (your worshippers) urge you by their devotions (to bring the deities to their sacrifices); adorable Agni, they (the deities), have genitive rated you, immortal, divine, all-wise, as the present divinity among men; they have genitive rated you as the all-present and all-wise deity.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The emulous gods: samanyavo dev─Бsas tvam nyerire: samanyavaс╕е = spardham─Бnaс╕е, viewing with. In this and he next verse, there is a repetition at the end of the line of three or four preceding words; thus, adevam janata pracetasam, vi┼Ыvam adevam janata pracetasam, with a slight modification of meaning in the repetition

+Jamison Brereton

You, o Agni, the god, did the gods of equal fervor install for always as the spoked wheel (of the sacrifice)тАФ
with such a purpose did they install you:
[Gods addressing mortals:] тАЬSacrifice to the immortal [=Agni] among the mortals; beget the god god-directed and discerning;
beget each one [=every new fire] as god-directed and discerning.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Hymn-introductory h├н is difficult to render. It does not have its normal causal sense, though perhaps in this position h├н is meant to explain why the hymn is recited following a particular ritual action. It is noteworthy that the first hymn of Maс╣Зс╕Нala VI (also, of course, to Agni) opens in exactly the same way: tv├бс╣Г h├н agne.

With Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) I take p─Бdas def as the direct address of the gods to mortals, with the speech introduced by ├нti kr├бtv─Б in c. (This idea goes back to Bergaigne; see Oldenberg SBE ad loc.) Rejecting this interpr., Oldenberg labors mightily to explain away the apparent 2nd pl. actives yajata and janata as voc. and 3rd pl. middle respectively. (In this he follows S─Бyaс╣Зa.) Renou tries in addition to make yajata also a 3rd pl. mid. (see also Gonda [Vedic Literature, 228], whose tr. renders both forms as 3rd plurals). Although yajata could actually be a voc., 3rd pl. middles in -ata to thematic stems are morphologically impossible, no matter how metrically unfavorable -anta would be.

GeldnerтАЩs direct speech interpr. solves these grammatical problems and also makes sense of the ├нti in c.

The poet plays with ─Б/a and the oppositional pair m├бrtya- / dev├б- in de, with chiastic #├бmartyam тАж m├бrtyeс╣гv ─Б╠Б# in d, and dev├бm ─Б╠Бdevam opening e. (See also dev─Б╠Бso dev├бm opening 1b.)

+Oldenberg

Thee, O Agni, the gods concordantly have ever set to work as their divine steward; with this intention 1 they have set thee to work. They have generated 2 thee, O worshipful one 2, the immortal among the mortals, the wise, god-loving god; they have generated every wise, god-loving (Agni) 3.

+Geldner

Dich, Agni, den Gott, haben ja die G├╢tter jederzeit einm├╝tig zu ihrem Wagenlenker bestellt, in diesem Sinne bestellt: Verehret den Unsterblichen unter den Sterblichen, erzeuget den g├╢tterfreundlichen Gott, den Verst├дndigen, den ganz g├╢tterfreundlichen Gott, den Verst├дndigen, den ganz g├╢tterfreundlichen erzeuget, den Verst├дndigen!

+Grassmann

Dich Agni haben als den Opferbringer stets den Gott die G├╢tter eines Sinnes eingesetzt (so dich mit Weisheit eingesetzt); Bei Sterblichen verehret den Unsterblichen, erzeugt den Gott, den weisheitsvollen G├╢tterfreund (erzeugt den steten weisheitsvollen G├╢tterfreund.)

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬBring to the presence of the worshippers, Agni, your brother Varuс╣Зa, as a participator fo the sacrifice, with a willing mind, the elder participator of the sacrifice; the ruler of the water, the ─Аditya, the supporter of men the sovereign venerated by mankind.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Agni, turn here to your brother Varuс╣Зa, to the gods with your favorтАФto him who yearns for sacrifice,
your oldest (brother) who yearns for sacrifice,
the truthful son of Aditi who supports the settled domains, the king who supports the settled domains.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

As Arnold (VedMetre, 300) suggests (so also Oldenberg, Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition), deleting agne in p─Бda a and reading vavс╣Ыtsu va (as in 3a) yields a fine Jagat─л line.

+Griffith

As such, O Agni, bring with favour to the Gods thy Brother Varuna who loveth sacrifice,
True to the Law, the Aditya who supporteth men, the King, supporter of mankind.

+Oldenberg

Do thou, [O Agni 1,] turn to brother Varuna, towards the gods 2 with thy kindness 3, to (Varuna) who accepts the sacrifice, to the eldest (god) who accepts the sacrifice, the righteous ├Вditya who supports the (human) tribes, the king who supports the (human) tribes.

+Geldner

Wende dich, Agni, an deinen Bruder Varuna, gn├дdig an die G├╢tter, an Varuna, der auf das Opfer eifers├╝chtig ist, der als Oberster auf das Opfer eifers├╝chtig ist, an den gesetzliebenden, v├╢lkerregierenden Aditisohn, an den v├╢lkerregierenden K├╢nig.

+Grassmann

Und f├╝hr, o Agni, deinen Bruder Varuna den G├╢ttern zu, mit Huld den opferliebenden, (den besten, opferliebenden); Den heiligen Aditja, der die Menschen sch├╝tzt (den K├╢nig, der die Menschen sch├╝tzt.)

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬFriendly and beautiful (Agni), bring your friend (Varruс╣Зa) to our presence, as two strong horses convey the swift chariot along the road to its goal; you receive, Agni, the gratifying (oblation) together with Varuс╣Зa, and with the all-illuminig Maruts; grant, brilliant Agni, happiness to our sons and grandsons; grant, beautiful Agni, happiness to ourselves.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

O comrade, turn to your comrade, like a wheel to a swift (horse), like chariotry at speed,
for us, o wondrous one, at speed.
Agni, you (will) find grace in company with Varuс╣Зa, with the all-radiant Maruts.
To press out progeny, o blazing one, make luck; for us, wondrous one, make luck.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The injunc. vidaс╕е is functionally multivalent, but usually interpr. as an impv.

(so Geldner, Renou, though not Witzel Got┼Н). On this form see comm. ad I.42.7-9 and IX.20.3. I would now allow an alternative translation as impv.: тАЬfind grace тАжтАЭ The final p─Бda (g) is a combination of the opening of c (asm├бbhyam dasma) and the ending of f (┼Ы├бс╣Г kс╣Ыdhi).

+Griffith

Do thou, O Friend, turn hither him who is our Friend, swift as a wheel, like two car-steeds in rapid course, Wondrous! to us in rapid course.
O Agni, find thou grace for us with Varuna, with Maruts who illumine all.
Bless us, thou Radiant One, for seed and progeny, yea, bless us, O thou Wondrous God.

+Oldenberg

O friend, turn to thy friend (Varuna), as a wheel of a chariot 1 rapidly (follows) the swift (horse), for our sake, O wonderful one, rapidly. O Agni, find mercy (for us) with Varuna, with the all-brilliant Maruts. Bless (us), O flaming one, that we may propagate ourselves, that we may press onward; bless us, O wonderful one!

+Geldner

O Freund! Drehe dich dem Freunde wie das Rad dem Rennpferd zu wie die Wagenr├дder in rascher Fahrt, f├╝r uns, du Meister, in rascher Fahrt! Agni, finde Gnade vor Varuna, vor den allgl├дnzenden Marut! Bring Gl├╝ck zur Fortpflanzung des Samens, du Brennender; bring uns Gl├╝ck, du Meister!

+Grassmann

Ihn den Genossen wende her, Genosse du, so wie ein rasches Wagenrad in schnellem Lauf (uns, herrlicher, in schnellem Lauf) O Agni schenk’ mit Varuna uns G├╢tterhuld, (mit Marut’s, den allgl├дnzenden) F├╝r Kind und Enkel schaffe Heil, o leuchtender (uns schaffe Heil, o herrlicher.)

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay you Agni, who are wise, avert from us the wrath of the divine Varuс╣Зa; do you, who are the most frequent sacrificer, the most diligent bearer (of oblations), the most resplendent liberate us from all animosities.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

You, Agni, knowing oneтАФfor us may you please placate through prayer the anger of god Varuс╣Зa. As best sacrificer, best conveyor (of oblations), constantly blazing,
release all hatreds from us.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

My тАЬmay you please placateтАЭ is meant to capture the precative (├бva) y─Бsis─лс╣гс╣нh─Бс╕е of the siс╣г-aorist to тИЪy─Б. Note the dissimilation (if thatтАЩs what it is) of the middle sibilant from expected rukified с╣г to plain s.

Note the phonetic figure straddling the hemistich boundary: b y─Бsis─лс╣гс╣нh─Бс╕е / c y├бjiс╣гс╣нhaс╕е.

In 4c, likewise 6b, Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition note the caesura after three (4c y├бjiс╣гс╣нho v├бhnitamaс╕е, 6b dev├бsya citr├бtam─Б). I wonder if the splv. suffix -tama- here is semi-detachable for metrical purposes, yielding an opening of 5 in both cases.

+Griffith

Do thou who knowest Varuna, O Agni, put far away from us the God’s displeasure.
Best Sacrificer, brightest One, refulgent remove thou far from us all those who hate us.

+Oldenberg

Mayst thou, O Agni, who knowest Varuna, deprecate for us the god’s anger. Being the best sacrificer, the best carrier (of the gods), flaming, remove from us all hatred.

+Geldner

Als Kundiger m├╢gest du, Agni, den Groll des Gottes Varuna f├╝r uns abbitten. Du, der beste Opferer und Fahrer, hellbrennend, nimm von uns alle Feindschaften!

+Grassmann

Du, der’s versteht, o Agni, m├╢gest wenden hinweg den Zorn uns Varuna’s, des Gottes, Als bester Opfrer und Verehrer strahlend, mach los von uns die Widersacher alle.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬDo you Agni our preserver bemost nigh to us with your protection at the breaking of this dawn; deprecate Varuс╣Зa for us and propitiated (by our praise) feed upon the grateful (oblation), and be to us of auspicious invocation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 21.4; Deprecate Varuс╣Зa for us: ava yakс╣гva no varuс╣Зam: vin─Б┼Ыaya, destroy (verb); varuс╣Зa-kс╣Ыtam (object), that which has been done by Varuс╣Зa, as disease inflicted by him, such as dropsy; or the term may imply p─Бpam, sin

+Jamison Brereton

You, Agni, come down close to us with your help; be nearest to us at the breaking of this dawn.
Through sacrifice placate Varuс╣Зa for us, as you give to us. Pursue his grace; be easy for us to invoke.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The idiom ├бva тИЪy─Б тАШplacate, appeaseтАЩ found in 4b finds a close variant in 5c ├бva yakс╣гva тАШplacate through sacrificeтАЩ to ├бva тИЪyaj. Though belonging to different roots, they are phonologically and semantically similar. Another such variant is found in d v─лh├н mс╣Ыс╕╖─лk├бm тАЬpursue his grace,тАЭ which echoes 3d mс╣Ыс╕╖─лk├бm тАж vidaс╕е тАЬyou (will) find graceтАЭ – again two different roots (v─л and vid) but phonologically and semantically similar.

+Griffith

Be thou, O Agni, nearest us with succour, our closest Friend while now this Morn is breaking.
Reconcile to us Varuna, be bounteous enjoy the gracious juice; be swift to hear us.

+Oldenberg

As such, O Agni, be for us the lowest 1 (god) with thy help, our nearest (friend) while this dawn shines forth. Being liberal (towards us), cause, by sacrificing, Varuna to go away from us. Love mercy; readily hear our call.

+Geldner

Sei du, Agni, uns nahe mit deiner Hilfe, uns der N├дchste bei dem Aufgang dieser Morgenr├╢te. Vers├╢hne bereitwillig den Varuna mit uns, sei zur Barmherzigkeit geneigt, sei f├╝r uns leicht zu errufen!

+Grassmann

Mit H├╝lfe sei, o Agni, uns der n├дchste, der liebste Freund beim Lichte dieses Fr├╝hroths; Bes├дnftige den Varuna uns huldvoll, verschaff uns Gunst, lass gern von uns dich rufen.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe glance of this auspicious deity, directed towards men, is most excellent, most wonderful, acceptable (to all) as the pure warm butter (from the milk) of the cow (is acceptable) to the deity; as the gift of a cow (is to a man).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Of this well-portioned god here his manifestation is the fairest, the most brilliant one among mortals.
Gleaming like the heated ghee of the inviolable (cow), (the
manifestation) of the god is eagerly sought like the largesse of a
milk-cow.

+Griffith

Excellent is the glance, of brightest splendour, which the auspicious God bestows on mortals-
The God’s glance, longed-for even as the butter, pure, heated, of the cow, the milch-cow’s bounty.

+Oldenberg

His, the fortunate god’s, appearance is excellent, and most brilliant among mortals. Like the bright, heated butter of the cow (the appearance) of the god is lovely, like the bountifulness of a milch-cow.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThese are the supreme, true, and desirable births of this divine Agni, invested (with radiance) in the unbounded (firmament); pure, bright, radiant lord (of all), may he come (to our) sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Births of Agni: As Agni, V─Бyu and S┼лrya; or, itmay refer to the plural ces of his manifestation; or, earth, firmament, and heaven

+Jamison Brereton

Three times do these highest births of his come into existenceтАФthe eagerly sought births of the god Agni.
Enveloped within the limitless, he has come hereтАФa blazing flame, ever shining for the stranger.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I take santi saty─Б╠Бhere as an etym. figure, a phrasal verb meaning тАЬcome into existenceтАЭ (тАЬcome [to be] trueтАЭ), rather than taking santi as copula and saty─Б╠Бas a simple adj. with most tr. For one thing, pres. tense forms of тИЪas in main clauses are usually existentials, not copulas; for another tr├нs should mean тАШthree timesтАЩ, not тАШthreeтАЩ or тАШthreefoldтАЩ as a copular reading seems to require (e.g., Geldner тАЬDreifach sind diese seine h├╢chsten wahren (Geburten) тАжтАЭ). See also saty├бm astu in 18d. I am not sure which three occasions are being referred to, but possibly to the production of the three ritual fires – though esp. given the word param├б- тАШhighestтАЩ, it could be a cosmic reference.

I do not know what тАЬenveloped within the limitlessтАЭ (anant├й ant├бс╕е p├бriv─лtaс╕е) refers to. It may be the dense swirling smoke, lacking clear boundaries, that surrounds a fire, or it may be the unborn AgniтАЩs concealment in the kindling sticks – though itтАЩs hard to see how they would be anant├б-. It is also possible that this is a reference to the paridhi sticks that surround the ritual fire (see comm. ad IV.3.2 below); they would be тАЬendlessтАЭ because a circle has no end. Note the phonological play of (an)ant├й ant├бс╕е, despite their different etymological affiliations.

In d the standard tr. take ari y├бс╕е as nom. sg. to the thematic stem ary├б- (e.g., Geldner тАШHerrтАЩ). I follow Thieme (Fremdling, 77-78) in interpr. it as gen. sg. to ar├н-.

Among other things, as Grassmann points out, this would be the only ex. of ary├б- with distraction, while ar├н- does have a few other distracted forms. There is no compelling formulaic evidence either way, but V.34.9 ket├║m ary├бс╕е тАЬthe beacon for the stranger,тАЭ adduced by Thieme, resembles our passage thematically.

+Griffith

Three are those births, the true, the most exalted, eagerly longed-for, of the God, of Agni.
He came invested in the boundless region, pure, radiant, friendly, mightily resplendent.

+Oldenberg

Three 1 are those highest, true, and lovely births of this god Agni. Being enveloped in the infinite 2 he has come hither, the bright, brilliant, shining Aryan.

+Geldner

Dreifach sind diese seine h├╢chsten wahren Geburten, die ersehnten Geburten des Gottes Agni. In endlosem Dunkel verh├╝llt ist er gekommen, der reine, helle, erstrahlende Herr.

+Grassmann

Dreifach ist dieses Gottes Agni Ursprung, der wahre, h├╢chste, der begehrungswerthe; Im unbegrenzten Raum verh├╝llet kam er, mit lichtem Glanz der treue hell erstrahlend.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe messenger, the invoker (of the gods), riding in a golden chariot with a tongue of flame, he frequents all the chambers (of sacrifice); drawn by red horses embodied resplendent, always agreeable, as a delling well supplied with food.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

As messenger he strives toward all seats, the Hotar whose chariot is golden, whose tongue is amid the pleasures [=oblations],
whose horses are ruddy, he wondrous, far-radiant, always pleasurable like a banquet abounding in food.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In b the caesura appears to coincide with a compound seam (#h├│t─Б h├нraс╣Зya/ratho тАж), as Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition also note. This is reminiscent of the proposed caesuras in 4c and 6b, before the splv. suffix -tama. See also 19b.

The first cmpd member r├бс╣Гsu- is taken by Schindler (Rt Nns, 40) as the loc. pl. to a root noun r├бn- тАШFreudeтАЩ, an analysis accepted by Mayrhofer (EWA s.v. RAс╣Ж).

+Griffith

This envoy joyeth in all seats of worship, borne on his golden car, sweet-tongued Invoker:
Lovely to look on, with red steeds, effulgent, like a feast rich in food, joyous for ever.

+Oldenberg

He, the messenger, longs for all seats, the Hotri with the golden chariot, with the lovely tongue, with the red horses, of marvellous appearance, brilliant, always lovely like an assembly abundant in food.

+Geldner

Er, der Bote, strebt allen Sitzen zu, der Hotri mit goldenem Wagen und erg├╢tzlicher Zunge, mit roten Rossen, stattlich, ergl├дnzend, immer erfreulich wie eine speisereiche Tafel.

+Grassmann

Als Bote strebt er hin zu allen Sitzen, mit goldnem Wagen, holder Zung’ als Priester, Mit rothen Rossen wundersch├╢n und strahlend, erfreuend stets wie reich besetzte Tafel.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAssociated with sacrifice, and knowing those men (who are engaged in good works), they lead him with the strong cord (of praise); he, the divine Agni, fulfilling (all desires), abides in the dwelling of this mortal, and obtains fellowhip in his wealth.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

He makes men perceive [=instructs them], as their tie to the sacrifice of Manu; they lead him forth with a great halter.
He dwells peacefully in his houses, assuring success; the god attains the fellowship of the mortal.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I follow Geldner (n. 9a) in giving m├бnuс╣гaс╕е a double reading, acc. pl. obj. of cetayan and gen. sg. dependent on yaj├▒├бbandhuс╕е. Note that it is neatly positioned between those two words.

I think yaj├▒├бbandhuс╕е has a more specific sense than simply тАШOpfergenosseтАЩ.

Rather, Agni is literally our тАШtieтАЩ (b├бndhu-) to the primal sacrifice instituted by Manu because he has always been present, always the same, at every sacrifice since then.

The referent of asya in c is taken as the mortal (m├бrta-) in d by Geldner (implicitly also Renou), as Agni by Witzel Got┼Н. Either is possible, both grammatically and contextually.

There is no requirement that a possessive coreferential with the subject be expressed by a reflexive (sv├бsya in this case), and though, technically speaking, an unaccented oblique form of ay├бm should have an antecedent, the close proximity of m├бrtasya and the fact that the subject of the preceding verb (nayanti), though pl., is clearly mortal would make asya = mortal unproblematic. And given the ritual intimacy of Agni and his worshipper(s), the house belongs to both.

Note the phonological echo in s─Б╠Бdhan (c) and sadhanitv├бm (d), even though they are semantically unconnected. As for the latter, I now favor the alternative deriv.

proposed by Scarlatta (291), from a base *sadhan├н- тАШTeilhaber am gemeinsam Schatz, Teilgaber, GenosseтАЩ in turn built to sa-dh├бna- (┼ЪB) тАШgemeinsamer SchatzтАЩ – rather than as a derivative of the [/a] root-noun cmpd sadha-n─л╠Б-, with shortening of the root vowel before -tv├б- (so AiG II.2.715). See sadhany├аm in X.50.3. In fact some or all of the three forms assigned to the root-noun cmpd by Grassmann (IV.4.14, VI.51.3, X.93.5) may also belong rather to GrassmannтАЩs stem sadhany├а-. (Both Lubotsky and Scarlatta assign all four forms [that is, incl. X.50.3] to the sadhan─л╠Б-, though, as just noted, Scarlatta considers the alternative analysis.) The problem with the root-noun analysis is that the semantic connection between тИЪn─л тАШleadтАЩ and the apparent sense of the derivative is quite attenuated. It is, however, the case here that two finite forms of тИЪn─л (nayanti 9b, nayatu 10a) flank sadhanitv├бm, so there may be at least a secondary connection perceived.

+Griffith

Allied by worship, let him give man knowledge: by an extended cord they lead him onward.
He stays, effectual in this mortal’s dwelling, and the God wins a share in his possessions.

+Oldenberg

He, the kinsman of sacrifice, has enlightened men 1. They lead him forward by a great rope 2. He dwells in his (the mortal’s) dwelling, accomplishing (his task). The god has obtained the companionship of the mortal.

+Geldner

Als der Opfergenosse des Manu erleuchtet er die Menschen. Ihn f├╝hren sie zum Altar am gro├Яen Lichtseil. Er wohnt, die Opfer ausrichtend, in dessen Behausung. Der Gott hat G├╝tergemeinschaft mit den Sterblichen erlangt.

+Grassmann

Das Opfer liebend trieb er an die Menschen; sie leiten vorw├дrts ihn am grossen Z├╝gel; Er wohnet segnend in des Menschen H├дusern, es fand der Gott des Sterblichen Gemeinschaft.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay that wise Agni conduct us to that wealth which is desired by the devout; he whom all the immortals have created for (the performance of) sacred oblations, the most rresplendent, liberate us from all animosities.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Let Agni, knowing (the way), lead us to the treasure, which was apportioned to him by the gods.
(The treasure) which all the immortals created with their insight, which Father Heaven as begetter (created)тАФ(that) they sprinkled (so it
became) real.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In b I follow Hoffmann (Injunk., 175) in taking the rel. clause as dev├бbhaktaс╣Г y├бd asya, rather than just y├бd asya with the standard tr. The sense doesnтАЩt differ markedly.

More difficult is the configuration of cd. All the standard interpr. (incl.

Hoffmann), save for Oldenberg (both SBE and Noten), take final ukс╣гan as the voc. sg. of ukс╣г├бn- тАШoxтАЩ, referring to Agni. I prefer, with Oldenberg, to take ukс╣гan as a 3rd pl. injunc.

main-clause verb (тИЪukс╣г тАШsprinkleтАЩ), with the subj. the immortals of c. The image is of the gods first creating the treasure and then bringing it to life like a watered plant. In favor of the majority interpr, I must concede, is the common idiom saty├бm тИЪkс╣Ы тАШmake realтАЩ, which would in fact complement my interpr. of santi saty─Б╠Бin 7a, but I find a voc. address to Agni in the middle of 3rd ps. reff. to him (10ab, 11, not to mention vss. 6-9) awkward. Renou refers to тАЬlтАЩ├йtranget├й dтАЩun tel Voc.,тАЭ despite explicitly rejecting OldenbergтАЩs finite verb interpr. And what is the treasure? A slightly different phrase r├бtnam тАж dy├║bhaktam (rather than dev├бbhaktam as here) returns in vs. 18, where it seems to refer to the light of Dawn in the form of the cows released from the Vala cave; here I think it may be the light of the newly kindled ritual fire – and of course the lights of Dawn and the fire of the dawn ritual can be superimposed upon and identified with each other. If the light of the new fire is the primary referent in this vs., ukс╣гan тАШsprinkledтАЩ may refer to sprinkling ghee on the fire, which action would cause it to blaze up. The next vs. (11), which describes the birth of Agni, fits this interpr.

+Griffith

Let Agni -for he knows the way- conduct us to all that he enjoys of God-sent riches,
What all the Immortals have prepared with wisdom, Dyaus, Sire, Begetter, raining down true blessings.

+Oldenberg

May this Agni, the knowing one, lead us to the god-given treasure which belongs to him 1. That (treasure) which all the immortals have created by their thought, which Dyaus, the father, the begetter (has created): that real (treasure) they have besprinkled 2.

+Geldner

Dieser Agni soll uns doch, des Weges kundig, zu dem gottgeschenkten Kleinod f├╝hren, das ihm geh├╢rt, das alle Unsterblichen, der Vater und Erzeuger Himmel, nach deinem Sinne wahr machten, du Stier.

+Grassmann

Uns f├╝hre Agni, der des Weges kundig, zu gottertheiltem Schatze, der ihm eigen Was weisheitsvoll die G├╢tter alle schufen, gew├дhre Djaus der Vater und Erzeuger.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬHe is first engendered in the habitation (of the sacrificers); then upon his station, (the altar), the base of the vast firmament; without feet, without head, concealing his extremities, combining with smoke in the nest of the rain-cloud.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

He was born first in the dwelling places, at the base of this great realm, as his womb,
footless, headless, concealing his two ends, continually retracting (his limbs [=flames]), in the nest of the bull.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The vs. treats the birth of the ritual fire on earth, with the second hemistich describing the amorphous shape and constant motion of physical fire. That it has neither foot nor head (ap─Б╠Бd a┼Ы─лrс╣г─Б╠Б) presumably refers to the lack of consistent vertical definition of a flickering fire; тАЬconcealing its two endsтАЭ (guh├бm─Бno ├бnt─Б) is reminiscent of 7c тАЬenveloped within the limitlessтАЭ (anant├й ant├бс╕е p├бriv─лtaс╕е), and the explanations suggested there may apply here. In addition, the тАЬtwo endsтАЭ may be the non-existent foot and head just referred to.

+Griffith

In houses first he sprang into existence, at great heaven’s base, and in this region’s bosom;
Footless and headless, both his ends concealing, in his Bull’s lair drawing himself together.

+Oldenberg

He has been born in the dwellings as the first, at the bottom of the great (air) 1, in the womb of this air 2, footless, headless, hiding both his ends, drawing towards himself (his limbs?), in the nest of the bull 3.

+Geldner

Er ward zuerst in den Fl├╝ssen geboren, im Grunde des gro├Яen, im Scho├Яe dieses Dunkelraumes, ohne F├╝├Яe, ohne Kopf, seine beiden Enden versteckend im Neste des Stieres, die Glieder einziehend.

+Grassmann

Er ward zuerst geboren in den H├дusern, am Grund des Himmels, in dem Schooss des Luftraums, Fusslos und kopflos beide Erden bergend, sich innig schmiegend an des Stieres Lager.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬRadiance has first proceeded to you, (Agni), who are glorified by praise, in the womb of the water, in the nest of the rain-cloud; the seven attached (priests) have engendered (praise) to the showerer (of benefits), who desirable, ever young, embodied, and resplendent.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The troop [=Aс╣Еgirases] set forth first amid admiration to the womb of truth, to the nest of the bullтАФ
The eagerly sought youth, wondrous, far-radiant [=Agni]тАФthe seven dear ones [=Aс╣Еgirases or their music] begat (him) for the bull.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I am in agreement with most of the standard interpr. that the referent of the subj. of ab is the troop of Aс╣Еgirases, expressed by the neut. s-stem ┼Ы├бrdhaс╕е (pace Grassmann, who takes it as a thematic masc. nom. sg., referring to Agni, sim. Schmidt [Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra, 43 n.

21]), though this word generally refers to the Marut troop.

I part company with these interpr. with regard to the referent of c, however.

Most take this string of nom. sg. masc. adj. as further descriptors of the Aс╣Еgiras troop, while I think they refer to Agni. Agni and his births are referred to as sp─Бrh├бearlier in the hymn (6d, 7b); in 8c he is described as vapuс╣гy├▓ vibh─Б╠Бv─Б exactly as here.

The recycling of this characterizing vocabulary seems to me a clue that the subject has changed here from the first half of the vs: it would be perverse to repeat this phraseology with a referent other than the original Agni. Note also that y├║van- тАШyoungтАЩ is regularly used of Agni, and in the context of his birth the word is esp. apt.

I take this nominal clause (/subclause) as annunciatory of the gapped object of d.

Geldner, Renou, and Oldenberg (SBE) take janayanta in d as intrans. тАШbe bornтАЩ (e.g., Geldner тАЬDem Bullen wurden die sieben Freunde geborenтАЭ), but this medial form is a standard ex. of -anta replacement of the undercharacterized act. -an and is therefore transitive. See my тАЬVoice fluctuation in the Rig Veda: Medial 3rd plural -anta in active paradigms,тАЭ IIJ 21 (1979) 146-69. It is correctly interpr. by Hoffmann (Injunk., 176) and Witzel Got┼Н. The form is an injunctive, contra the Pp.; so already Grassmann; see Oldenberg (Noten), Hoffmann. The тАЬseven dear onesтАЭ (sapt├б priy─Б╠Бsaс╕е) are most likely the Aс╣Еgirases, here referred to in the plural rather than the collective neut. sg. in p─Бda a. III.31.5 contains тАЬseven inspired poetsтАЭ (sapt├б v├нpr─Бс╕е) in a clear Aс╣Еgiras/Vala context. It is also possible that the phrase refers to the Aс╣ЕgirasesтАЩ music, since sapt├б v─Б╠Бс╣З─лс╕е тАШseven voicesтАЩ is a common phrase. The adj. priy─Б╠Бsaс╕е could be either masc. or fem.

+Griffith

Wondrously first he rose aloft, defiant, in the Bull’s lair, the homeof holy Order,
Longed-for, young, beautiful, and far-resplendent: and sevendear frieuds sprang up unto the Mighty.

+Oldenberg

The host 1 came forth wonderfully at first, in the womb of Rita, in the nest of the bull 2, lovely and young, of marvellous appearance, and brilliant 3. Seven friends 4 were born for the bull.

Zuerst kam unter lautem Beifall die Schar hervor im Scho├Яe des Gesetzes, im Neste des Stiers, die ersehnte, jugendliche, stattliche, erstrahlende. Dem Bullen wurden die sieben Freunde geboren.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIn this world, our mortal forefathers departed after instrumental tuting the sacred rite, when, calling upon the dawn, they extricated the milk-yielding kine, concealed among the rocks in the darkness (of the cave).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Our mortal forefathers: the aс╣Еgirasas; the reference is to the origin of fire-worship by Aс╣Еgiras and his followers

+Jamison Brereton

Our forefathers here, belonging to Manu, stationed themselves in front, panting over the truth.
They [=the forefathers/Aс╣Еgirases] drove up those with a rock as their pen, the good milkers within the cave, the ruddy dawns being
called to.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This is the first of the Vala myth vss. As noted in the published introduction, the actors throughout must be the Aс╣Еgirases, but they are never named.

The curious phrase с╣Ыt├бm ─Б┼Ыuс╣г─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е тАЬpanting over the truthтАЭ occurs three times in IV.1-2 (also 2.14, 16). It expresses the energy and effort of the Aс╣Еgirases in singing the true song that opened the Vala cave and freed the cows. See L├╝ders (514-15).

The med. part. huv─Бn├б- is ordinarily passive in value; pace Grassmann, only VII.30.3 is clearly trans. I therefore take huv─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е here as fem. acc. pl. modifying uс╣г├бsaс╕е in passive sense. The standard interpr. is masc. nom. pl. in trans. value, тАШcalling toтАЩ.

This would of course make just as much sense; my choice is based on the usage of the preponderance of occurrences of the stem.

+Griffith

Here did our human fathers take their places, fain to fulfil the sacred Law of worship.
Forth drave they, with loud call, Dawn’s teeming Milch-kine bid in the mountainstable, in the cavern.

+Oldenberg

Here our human fathers have sat down 1, aspiring after Rita 2. Invoking the dawns 3, they have driven out the milch-cows which dwelt in the rock-stable, in the prison.

+Geldner

Unsere menschlichen V├дter setzten sich dazu hin, indem sie sich f├╝r das Rechte ereiferten. Die im Fels eingepferchten gutmilchenden K├╝he in der H├╢hle trieben sie heraus, die Morgenr├╢ten anrufend.

+Grassmann

Dort sassen unsre V├дter, hold den Menschen, ihm zugewandt, den heiligen entflammend; Sie f├╝hrten rufend aus die Morgenr├╢then, die reich an Milch in Felsenkluft verschlossnen.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬRending the rocks, they worshipped (Agni), and other (sages) taught everywhere their (acts); unprovided with the means of (extricating) the cattle, they glorified the author of success, whence they found the light, and were thus enabled (to worship him) with holy ceremonies.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

They [=the forefathers/Aс╣Еgirases] cleaned themselves, after having split the stone. This (deed) of theirs the others proclaimed all about.

Lacking ropes to hold the livestock, they sang the decisive act: тАЬThey found the light! They sought it with their insightful thoughts!тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Med. marmс╣Ыjata is most likely reflexive, as I and most other interpr. take it, though S─Бyaс╣Зa. and Renou supply Agni as object. Although the reflex. interpr. seems a little thin – splitting stone is dirty work, so they had to clean themselves up – Agni is out of place in this Vala context and there is no other obvious candidate to be object.

Moreover, the middle voice suggests a reflexive sense.

The referent of any├й in b is not clear to me. By my placement rules (see тАЬVedic any├б- ‘another, the other’: syntactic disambiguation,тАЭ Sound law and analogy, Fs. Beekes [ed. A. Lubotsky], 1997, pp. 111-18), it must be definite (тАЬthe othersтАЭ).

Most tr. take it as indefinite, though Hoffmann tr. it as definite and implicitly contrastive with the unspecified subject of p─Бda a: тАЬDie (einen) тАж Die anderen von ihnen тАжтАЭ I think this approach is the correct one, though I donтАЩt think we need or want the group of Aс╣Еgirases to be split into moieties. Instead, in my view, the contrastive groups are the primordial singers, the Aс╣Еgirases, and their modern counterparts, the poets and singers of the current ritual. The injunctive v├н vocan would allow a presential interpr. (тАЬthey proclaim тАжтАЭ) with current singers as subj.

instead of or in addition to the preterital one in the published translation

In c we return to the Aс╣Еgirases, whose singing opens the Vala cave – hence тАЬthey sang the decisive act.тАЭ Most tr. take k─Бr├б- as a victory song of some sort (the exception is Witzel Got┼Н: тАЬтАж singen sie auf das Schaffen,тАЭ where k─Бr├б- is the subject of the song. But I think the expression is more radical: as so often in the RV, our poet wants to emphasize the power of words to make things happen, the connection between song (the cause) and the act, the splitting of the rock (effect).

The hapax cmpd. pa┼Ыv├бyantra- is puzzling in formation and sense, although the parts it is based on are relatively clear. The 1st member is pa┼Ыu- тАШlivestockтАЩ or a derivative thereof, the 2nd is or contains yantr├б- тАШbinding ropeтАЩ. The interpr. comes down to deciding which is the lesser of two evils: positing an otherwise unattested extended stem pa┼Ыv├б- beside pa┼Ы├║- but a relatively conventional bahuvr─лhi тАШhaving binding ropes for the livestockтАЩ or rejecting the extended stem but ending up with an anomalously formed and accented bahuvr─лhi. Oldenberg argues strenuously for the former, with the rather cumbersome tr. тАЬin ihren Vorrichtungen zum Festhalten тАж das Vieh haltend,тАЭ and some version of this analysis is followed by Hoffmann and Witzel Got┼Н. Geldner and Renou (the latter with some hesitation) opt for the latter, with Geldner suggesting a reverse bahuvr─лhi (for ayantra-pa┼Ыu-). (He cagily fails to accent it.) In the end I swallow some version of the second analysis, primarily because I find it unlikely that such a common word as pa┼Ы├║- would display an unnecessary extended stem in just this place in all of Sanskrit, particularly because thereтАЩs little metrical advantage to it here. However, I do not follow GeldnerтАЩs reverse bahuvr─лhi interpr. (roughly, тАЬhaving livestock loosed from the binding ropesтАЭ), but assume that it is the Aс╣Еgirases who lack yantra-s to bind the cattle and do so with song instead. (This interpr. goes back to Bergaigne; see Oldenberg SBE ad loc.) That some form of verbal expression could serve as a yantr├б- is shown by the cmpd. ┼Ыl├│ka-yantra- (IX.73.6) тАШhaving ┼Ыlokas as binding ropesтАЩ. Unfortunately I do not see how to make this explanation work formally, particularly with regard to accent, esp. as there exists a differently accented privative cmpd. ayantr├б- in X.46.6. I leave it at this, unsatisfactorily.

In terms of the structure of the vs., I now think the odd p─Бdas (a, c) refer to the Aс╣Еgirases and the even ones (b, d) to the current singers. I would therefore slightly modify the published translation, which presents p─Бda d as if it were the direct speech – the song – of the Aс╣Еgirases described in c. I now think d is what the other, current poets were said to proclaim in b.

+Griffith

Splendid were they when they had rent the mountain: others, around, shall tell forth this their exploit.
They sang their song, prepared to free the cattle: they found the light; with holy hymns they worshipped.

+Oldenberg

Having rent the rock they cleaned themselves. Others around told forth that (deed) of theirs. Taking тАж as an instrument (?) 1, they sang triumphantly 2. They found the light; they chanted their prayers.

Sie putzten sich, nachdem sie den Fels aufgesprengt hatten. Andere erz├дhlten diese Tat von ihnen. Als ihre Herde der Schranken ledig war, sangen sie den Siegessang; sie fanden das Licht, nachdem sie in ihren Gedanken danach verlangt hatten.

+Grassmann

Sie schm├╝ckten sich, als sie gesprengt den Felsen; dies Werk der V├дter priesen rings die andern; Die Heerde leitend sangen Jubellied sie; den Lichtglanz findend flehten sie mit Andacht.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬDevoted to (Agni), those leaders (of sacred rites), with minds intent upon (recovering) the cattle, forced open, by (the power) of divine prayer, the obstructing, compact, solid mountain confining the cows, a cow-pen full of kine.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Those with their mind set on cattle (opened up) the solid, knotted-up, enclosing stone that held the cows.
The firmly fixed pen full of cows did the men, the fire-priests, open up with divine speech.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The hapax dс╣Ыdhr├б- is plausibly explained by Hoffmann (reported in EWA s.v.) as a crossing of a redupl. nominal*dadhr├б- (тИЪdhс╣Ы) and the ppl. dс╣Ыс╕Нha (тИЪdс╣Ыh), the latter found in the second hemistich (15c).

+Griffith

Eager, with thought intent upon the booty, the men with their celestial speech threw open,
The solid mountain firm, compact, enclosing, confining Cows, the stable full of cattle.

+Oldenberg

Longing for the cows in their mind, those men, the Usigs 1, have opened with godly words the fast-holding, closed rock, which enclosed and encompassed the cows, the firm stable full of cows.

+Geldner

Das Herz voll Verlangen nach K├╝hen haben die M├дnner, die Usij, den festen, zugesperrten Fels, der die Rinder festhielt und umschlo├Я, den gefestigten Rinderpferch mit g├╢ttlichem Wort erschlossen.

+Grassmann

Sie thaten auf mit beutelust’gem Sinne den Fels, der fest die K├╝he hielt umschlossen, Den dicht umhegten, festen Stall der K├╝he die M├дnner eifrig durch den Spruch der G├╢tter.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThey first have comprehended the name of the kine, knowing the thrice seven excellent (forms) or the maternal (rhythm); then they glorified the conscious dawns and the purple dawn appeared with the radiance of the sun.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Comprehended the name of the kine: te manvata prathamam n─Бma dhenoс╕е: dhenoс╕е = v─Бk, speech and with n─Бma, stutis─Бdhakam ┼Ыabdam─Бtram, mere sound as the means of praise; the passage may also refer to the ancient nominative nclature of cattle, as uttered by the Aс╣Еgirasas: ehi surabhi, guggulu, gandhini; thrice seven: twenty one metres of the vedas

+Jamison Brereton

They brought to mind the first name of the milk-cow; thrice seven highest (names) of the mother they found.
(The cows) recognizing it [=the name], bellowed out (to the men), (like) maidens (announcing their bridegroom choice). The ruddy one
[=Dawn] became manifest with the glorious (name) of the cow.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In the published translation pratham├бm in the phrase t├й manvata pratham├бс╣Г n─Б╠Бma is rendered as an adj. with n─Б╠Бma (тАЬthe first nameтАЭ). On the basis of VI.1.a tv├бm тАж pratham├│ man├│t─Б тАЬyou (were) the first minderтАЭ I think it possible (but not certain) that pratham├бm here is an adverb: тАЬthey first brought to mind the name тАжтАЭ The agent noun man├│tar- is built to the verb stem manu- found in our passage, and pratham├бm may qualify the action of тАШbringing to mindтАЩ rather than the name brought to mind.

A comma should be inserted in the published translation after тАЬ(The cows)тАЭ in p─Бda c.

On vr─Б╠Б- see comm. ad VIII.2.16 and Jamison 2003 (= тАЬVedic vr─Б╠Б: evidence for the svayaс╣Гvara in the Rig Veda?тАЭ in Paitim─Бna: Essays in Iranian, IndoEuropean, and Indian Studies in Honor of Hanns-Peter Schmidt, vols. 1-2 [ed.

Siamak Adhami], 2003, pp. 39-56).

Because of its accentuation ya┼Ы├бs─Б should be adjectival; the question is what head noun to supply. Flg. L├╝ders (Varuс╣Зa, 521, also fld. by Hoffmann, Witzel Got┼Н), I supply тАШnameтАЩ, which appears in p─Бda a and appears to be the topic of the rest of the vs. Geldner and Oldenberg prefer тАШmilkтАЩ, but this is contextually less likely.

+Griffith

The Milch-cow’s earliest name they comprehended: they found the Mother’s thrice-seven noblest titles.
This the bands knew, and sent forth acclamation:with the Bull’s sheen the Red One was apparent.

+Oldenberg

They have devised the first name of the milch-cow; they have found the three times seven highest (names or essences) of the mother 1. The hosts 2, understanding this, acclaimed. The red one 3 became visible through the brilliant (milk?) 4 of the cow.

+Geldner

Sie erinnerten sich an den ersten Namen der Kuh, sie fanden die dreimal sieben h├╢chsten Namen der Mutter. Diesen verstehend antworteten die lockenden K├╝he mit Gebr├╝ll. Die Morgenr├╢te kam zum Vorschein mit dem, was die Zierde der Kuh ausmacht.

+Grassmann

Sie nahmen wahr der Milchkuh ersten Namen, die dreimal sieben herrlichsten der Mutter. Erkennend dies, frohlockten laut die Scharen, und hell erschien durch Glanz der Kuh das Fr├╝hroth

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe scattered darkness was destroyed; the firmament glowed with radiance; the lustre of the divine dawn arose; then the sun stood above the undecaying mountains, beholding all that was right or wrong among mankind.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The bilious darkness disappeared; heaven lightened; the radiance of the goddess Dawn arose.
The Sun mounted the lofty fields, looking upon the straight and the crooked among mortals.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On n├й┼Ыat as a replacement for an original thematic redupl. aor. with radical zero-grade (expected *na-n┼Ы-a-), with the vocalism of the first syllable replaced by that of the weak perfect, see Hoffmann, Injunk. 64-65.

On d├║dhita-, a qualifier of darkness, see EWA s.v., with ref. to Schindler (1967), who separates it from dudhr├б-, etc., and adduces possible Germanic and Toch. color-term cognates.

+Griffith

The turbid darkness fled, the heaven was sp, endid! up rose the bright beam of celestial Morning.
Surya ascended to the wide expanses, beholding deeds of men both good and evil.

+Oldenberg

The confused 1 darkness disappeared; the sky appeared in splendour; the shine of the goddess Dawn rose up. The Sun ascended to the wide plains, beholding right and wrong deeds among the mortals.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThereupon awaking, the (Aс╣Еgirasas) beheld (the cattle set free), and seized upon the precious treasures; the universal gods then came to all (their) dwellings; Mitra and Varuс╣Зa may your truth be (kept) to him who worships (you).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

And then afterward having awakened they looked about; and then they held up the treasure apportioned by heavenтАФ
all the gods (did so) in all the houses. O Mitra, Varuс╣ЗaтАФlet it
[=treasure] come into existence (also) for our insightful thought.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I interpr. the тАЬtreasure apportioned by heavenтАЭ (r├бtnam тАж dy├║bhaktam) to be in the first instance cows (as in I.73.6), those released from the Vala cave, but the cows conceived of as dawns and therefore as light, including the light of the newly kindled ritual fire. See vs. 10 above, with r├бtnam тАж dev├бbhaktam. This buried тАЬlightтАЭ motif works well with the houses in p─Бda c, where the ritual fire is at home (see vss.

9, 11 above), and provides an easy transition to the invocation of Agni in the next vs. The subj. of dh─Бrayanta in b I take as the gods in c (with Oldenberg, SBE, Hoffmann, Witzel Got┼Н), rather than taking c as a separate nominal cl. (Geldner, Renou). Note the chiastic morphological figure in c, allowing alliteration between the nom./loc. pairs: v├н┼Ыve v├н┼Ыv─Бsu d├║ry─Бsu dev─Б╠Б(с╕е).

In d I supply the treasure (in the form of light) as the subj. of saty├бm astu (so also Hoffmann). This VP should be interpr. in the context of santi saty─Б╠Бin 7a. See comm. there.

+Griffith

Then, afterwards they looked around, awakened, when first they held that Heaven allotted treasure.
Now all the Gods abide in all their dwellings. Varuna, Mitra, be the prayer effective.

+Oldenberg

Then, afterwards, being awoke they looked around; then they took that treasure given by Heaven, all the gods in all the houses. O Mitra, may true (fulfilment) belong to (our) prayer, O Varuna!

+Geldner

Da, als sie hernach erwacht waren, blickten sie um sich; da hielten sie das himmelgeschenkte Kleinod fest: “Alle G├╢tter sind in allen H├дusern”. Dem Wunsche soll Erf├╝llung werden, o Mitra und Varuna!

+Grassmann

Da erst erwachend leuchteten fortan sie, da erst erhielten sie den Schatz des Himmels, Die G├╢tter all’ in allen ihren St├дtten; erf├╝llt die Bitte, Varuna und Mitra.

рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рд╢реБрд╢реБрдЪрд╛рдирдВ рднреГрд╢рдВ рджреАрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдВ рд╣реЛрддрд╛рд░рдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдорд╛рд╣реНрд╡рд╛рддрд╛рд░рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рднрд░рд╕рдореН рдЖрд╣реБрддрд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдкреНрд░рджрд╛рдиреЗрди рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдкреЛрд╖рдХрдВ рдпрдЬрд┐рд╖реНрдардВ рдпрд╖реНрдЯреГрддрдордореН рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛рдореН рдЕрдЪреНрдЫ рдЕрднрд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдп рд╡реЛрдЪреЗрдп рд╕реНрддрд╡рд╛рдирд┐ ред рдЧрд╡рд╛рдореН рдКрдзрдГ рд╢реБрдЪрд┐ рд╢реБрджреНрдзрдВ рдкрдпрдГ рди рдЕрддреГрдгрддреН ред рддрд╡рд╛рд╣реБрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердВ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдиреЛ рди рджреЛрдЧреНрдзрд┐ ред рдЕрдВрд╢реЛрдГ рд╕реЛрдорд▓рддрд╛рдЦрдгреНрдбрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐ рдЕрдиреНрдзрдГ рд░рд╕рд╛рдЦреНрдпрдордиреНрдирдВ рдкреВрддрдВ рджрд╢рд╛рдкрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░реЗрдг рд╢реЛрдзрд┐рддрдВ рд╕рддреН рди рдкрд░рд┐рд╖рд┐рдХреНрддрдореН ред рдЧреГрд╣реЗрд╖реБ рди рдкреНрд░рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрддрдореНред рдХрд┐рдВрддреНрд╡рдиреЗрди рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдиреЗрди рдХреЗрд╡рд▓рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рд░реЗрд╡ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ" рее рд╡реЛрдЪреЗрдп ред рдмреНрд░реВрдЮрдГ рдЖрд╢реАрд░реНрд▓рд┐рдВрдЩрд┐ тАШрдмреНрд░реБрд╡реЛ рд╡рдЪрд┐рдГ’ред рд▓рд┐рдЩреНрдпрд╛рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдпрдЩреН’ред тАШ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реНрдпреБрднрдпрдерд╛ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рд╛рд░реНрд╡рдзрд╛рддреБрдХрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рд╕реАрдпреБрдЯрдГ рд╕рд▓реЛрдкрдГ ред рдЕрддреГрдгрддреН ред тАШрдЙрддреГрджрд┐рд░реН рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд╛рдирд╛рджрд░рдпреЛрдГ ред рджреЛрд╣рдирдореЗрд╡ рдКрдзреЛрд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдирдореН ред рдкрд░рд┐рд╖рд┐рдХреНрддрдореН ред рд╕рд┐рдЮреНрдЪрддреЗрдГ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд┐ рдХреНрддрдГ ред тАШрдЙрдкрд╕рд░реНрдЧрд╛рддреНрд╕реБрдиреЛрддрд┐’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рд╖рддреНрд╡рдореН ред’ рдЧрддрд┐рд░рдирдиреНрддрд░рдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЧрддреЗрдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд░рдГ рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay I glorify the present radiant Agni, the invoker (of the gods), the supporter of the universe, most deserving of adoration, without milking the pure udder (of the cow), without the purified food of the Soma offered in libation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Without the purified food: i.e., no offering is made to Agni on the occasion; praise alone is addressed to him

+Jamison Brereton

I would call here blazing Agni as Hotar, the best sacrificer who carries all burdens.
He drilled, seemingly, the gleaming udder of the cows, which was
purified like the stalk of the plant poured in circles [=soma].

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In b Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition note a caesura after 3; I wonder instead whether the caesura comes at the cmpd seam (#h├│t─Бraс╣Г vi┼Ыv├б/bharasaс╣Г тАж), a solution they themselves suggest for 8b, where the caesura would otherwise come after 2. See also 4c, 6b.

On the cmpd vi┼Ыv├б-bharas- see comm. ad V.54.10.

The general opinion is surely correct, that the тАЬgleaming udder of the cowsтАЭ (┼Ы├║cy ┼л╠Бdhaс╕е тАж g├бv─Бm) stands for the cowsтАЩ milk, which is compared to the soma stalk, itself standing for soma. But I think that the udder also stands for the Vala cave, which contained the cows. The root тИЪtс╣Ыd тАШdrillтАЩ is used for breaching the Vala cave in VI.17.1, 3, X.74.4. Geldner finds the subj. of atс╣Ыс╣Зat unclear, but surely Agni makes the most sense (not the sacrificer, per S─Бyaс╣Зa.). In his ritual role, Agni causes the dawn to dawn and therefore opens up the Vala cave on a daily basis. And at the same time he brings the outpouring of ghee (in the sacrifice) and the morning dakс╣гiс╣З─Б and other products of the cow.

The two soma-related terms aс╣Г┼Ы├║- and ├бndhas- are difficult to define and to distinguish from each, esp. since both can be used in place of soma itself. However, insofar as itтАЩs possible to tell, they seem to refer to (parts of) the physical plant soma, rather than its product, the juice also called soma. As far as I know, this is the only passage in which the two terms occur together, with gen. aс╣Г┼Ы├│с╕е dependent on acc. ├бndhaс╕е, which suggests that ├бndhas- is a part of the aс╣Г┼Ы├║-. This surmise supports the interpr. given by EWA s.vv. (with lit.) that the aс╣Г┼Ы├║- is the plant and ├бndhas- is the plantтАЩs stalk. The use of both terms to refer loosely to the soma drink is similar to the use of тАШgrapeтАЩ or тАШvineтАЩ to refer to wine. I do not understand the position of n├б. With the other standard interpr. I tr. it as if it qualifies the verb it immediately follows (тАЬhe drilled, seemingly тАжтАЭ; Geldner тАЬer zapfte gleichsam тАж,тАЭ etc.), but this is simply not a regular RVic usage: similes are always nominal. I would like to connect it with the double usage of ┼л╠Бdhaс╕е just discussed, but IтАЩm not sure how. I wonder if the 2nd reading of ┼л╠Бdhaс╕е as equivalent to the Vala cave hints at a simile like vraj├бm тАж g├бv─Бm iva тАЬlike a pen of cowsтАЭ (I.130.3; cf. I.10.7, IV.20.8, etc.). This would allow us to tr. the phrase тАЬHe drilled the gleaming udder of the cows [=milk] like the тАШudderтАЩ [=pen/Vala] of the cows,тАЭ which would restore n├б to its normal function of marking nominal similes.

+Griffith

I will call hither brightly-beaming Agni, the Herald, all-supporting, best at worship.
He hath disclosed, like the milch cows’ pure udder, the Sorria’s juice when cleansed and poured from beakers.

+Oldenberg

I will address flaming Agni, the Hotri, the supporter of everything 1, the best sacrificer. He has perforated, as it were, the pure udder of the cows, (and has made flow the milk) purified like the poured sap of the Soma shoots.

+Geldner

Ich m├╢chte den brennenden Agni herbitten als Hotri, der die ganze Last tr├дgt und am besten opfert. Er zapfte gleichsam das reine Euter der K├╝he an, das lauter wie der eingeschenkte Saft des Stengels.

+Grassmann

Nun ruf’ ich an den strahlenreichen Agni, der alles n├дhrt, am besten ehrt und opfert, Auf schloss er, wie der K├╝he lichtes Euter, wie einen Trank, den ausgegossnen Soma.

+Elizarenkova

рдЕрдпрдордЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд┐рдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд░реНрд╣рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдореН рдЕрджрд┐рддрд┐рдГред рдЕрджрд┐рддрд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╡рдорд╛рддрд╛ ред рддрджреНрд╡рджреНрджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреЛрд╖рдХ рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдорджрд┐рддрд┐рд░реНрднреВрд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреАрдпрдГ рдЖрдзрд╛рд░рднреВрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рдпрд╛рд╡рддреН ред рдЗрдпрдВ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдирд░рдГ’ (рддреИ. рдмреНрд░рд╛. рей.реп.резрен) рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реБрддреЗрдГред рддрдерд╛рдпрдордЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдорд╛рдиреБрд╖рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдореН рдЕрддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ рдЕрддрд┐рдерд┐рд╡рддреН рдкреВрдЬреНрдпреЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рджреЗрд╡рдирд╢реАрд▓рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреДрдгрд╛рдореН рдЕрд╡рдГ рдЕрдиреНрдирдВ рд╣рд╡рд┐рдГ рдЖрд╡реГрдгрд╛рдирдГ рд╕рдВрднрдЬрдиреН рдЬрд╛рддрд╡реЗрджрд╛рдГ ред рдЬрд╛рддрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдВ рд╡реЗрддреНрддреАрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рддрд╡реЗрджрд╛рдГ ред рд╕рдГ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреДрдгрд╛рдВ рд╕реБрдореГрд│реАрдХрдГ рд╕реБрдЦрдХрд░рдГ рднрд╡рддреБ рее рдЕрддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ ред рдЕрдд рд╕рд╛рддрддреНрдпрдЧрдордиреЗ ‘ред’ рдЛрддрдиреНрдпрдЮреНрдЬрд┐┬░’ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рдЗрдерд┐рдиреНрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ ред рдирд┐рддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╛рджреНрдпреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрдГ ред рдорд╛рдиреБрд╖рд╛рдгрд╛рдореН ред рдордиреЛрд░рдкрддреНрдпрд╛рдиреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ тАШрдордиреЛрд░реНрдЬрд╛рддрд╛рд╡рдЮреНрдпрддреМ рд╖реБрдХреНрдЪ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЕрдЮреНрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ ред рдЮрд┐рддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╛рджреНрдпреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрдГ реерее резрел рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay Agni be the Aditi of all those in whom sacrifice is offered; may he be the guest of all men; receiving the (sacrificial) food of the devout may he to whom all is known, be the bestower of felicity.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 33.16; may Agni be the Aditi: may he be the cherisher of the gods as if he were Aditi, their mother; or, Aditi may mean the earth, which is their stay or support;

Aditi = without a defect, gasyo khaс╣Зс╕Нanam n─Бsa adian, not mean or base; receiving the sacrificial food: dev─Бn─Бm ava avriс╣Зanaс╕е = participating in the sacrificial food of the worshippers; or, delivering oblations offered to the gods, i.e., through fire

+Jamison Brereton

As the Aditi of all those worthy of the sacrifice [=gods], the guest of all the sons of Manu [=men],
let Agni J─Бtavedas, choosing the aid of the gods, become very gracious.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Within the balanced phrases of the first hemistich – v├н┼Ыveс╣г─Бm ├бditir yaj├▒├нy─Бn─Бm, v├н┼Ыveс╣г─Бm ├бtithir m─Б╠Бnuс╣г─Бс╣З─Бm – the nearly identical nominatives ├бditir and ├бtithir make rhetorical sense. But why Agni is called, or identified as, Aditi (or boundlessness or innocence, if it is used as a common noun) is unclear. Since Aditi is the archetypal divine mother, perhaps Agni is being credited with a maternal relation to the gods, as a deliberate paradoxical foil to vs. 1, where the gods install Agni and are his de facto parents, and to the other accounts of his birth in this hymn. It is also the case that Agni is closely associated with Varuс╣Зa, a son of Aditi, early in the hymn (vss. 2, 3, 4, 5, also 18), though in vs. 2 it is explicitly stated that Agni is Varuс╣ЗaтАЩs younger brother, certainly not his mother. For a different wordplay involving ├бditisee IV.2.11 in the next hymn.

+Griffith

The freest God of all who should be worshipped, the guest who is received in all men’s houses,
Agni who hath secured the Gods’ high favour,-may he be gracious, to us Jatavedas.

He, the Aditi (i. e. the freedom) of all the worshipful gods, the guest 1 of all men, Agni, choosing (for us) the protection of all godsтАФmay he, G├вtavedas, be merciful.
